      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5812054928596936583">The Eddings give readers a guided tour through the extensive background material they used to create the world and people behind one of the great sagas of fantasy. In the process, they give the reader insight--and sometimes advice--on how to write big books that lots of people will read and enjoy.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer19415764">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5574477776978483472">Allow me to point out that this book is definitely not one to be read from start to finish. It's not that kind of book. <br /><br />This is the book that you read when you want to gain a full understanding of everything concerning the world and its history. This is where you turn for religious teachings, for currency names and exchange rates. <br /><br />If anyone ever decided that they wanted to make a game or a movie based on these books, then this is definitely the place that you want to look to get the specific inf</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5574477776978483472">Allow me to point out that this book is definitely not one to be read from start to finish. It's not that kind of book. <br /><br />This is the book that you read when you want to gain a full understanding of everything concerning the world and its history. This is where you turn for religious teachings, for currency names and exchange rates. <br /><br />If anyone ever decided that they wanted to make a game or a movie based on these books, then this is definitely the place that you want to look to get the specific information you would need to fully flesh out the world.<br /><br />Basically, this book contains all of the interesting details about the world that would seem rather boring or unnecessary to a typical reader of the books.<br /><br />So, as far as being a good read goes, this one just cannot even begin to compete. As far as being an interesting source of information about an excellent series, this is definitely top of the line material.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1691432701156203169">My considered opinion is that David Eddings is a little bit of a dick (and a little bit of a misogynist too, although I think he tries). <span id="freeTextContainer6702817312700866568">I find it impressive that they wrote this 460+ page book just to prepare for writing 10 others. As a fan of the original Belgariad and Mallorean, as well as both Polgara the Sorceress and Belgarath the Sorcerer, this "how to" process provided more insight than I initially expected. I found much of it fascinating, but think they could have pared down things like currency for the sake of publishing. Otherwise, a good read.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_63145031">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63145031" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1973239-jeremy-preacher" class="left imgcol" title="Jeremy Preacher"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1379094189p2/1973239.jpg" alt="Jeremy Preacher" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/63145031?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1973239-jeremy-preacher" class="user" title="Jeremy Preacher">Jeremy Preacher</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/953146.The_Rivan_Codex" title="Hardcover 9780345424020" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1973239-jeremy-preacher?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer63145031">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4918053445753890578">The Rivan Codex is actually quite entertaining, for what it is - a collection of notes and reference materials used in the creation of the Garion books, bookended by Eddings's firmly-stated opinions about how to go about writing a fantasy series. This was pure 'nip to me when I was a teenager - I am fascinated by the process of worldbuilding, and while large chunks of this are fairly dry, they're <em>interesting</em>, at least to me. (And the bits that aren't purely notes are largely written in the more</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4918053445753890578">The Rivan Codex is actually quite entertaining, for what it is - a collection of notes and reference materials used in the creation of the Garion books, bookended by Eddings's firmly-stated opinions about how to go about writing a fantasy series. This was pure 'nip to me when I was a teenager - I am fascinated by the process of worldbuilding, and while large chunks of this are fairly dry, they're <em>interesting</em>, at least to me. (And the bits that aren't purely notes are largely written in the more formal style that I think Eddings does reasonably well - the prose ends up being tighter and less digressive, and actually has some rhythm. Compare the origin of Belgarath here with the version in his eponymous book.)<br /><br />It was a little ironic that I felt this held up fairly well, when one of my big complaints of all of Eddings's work that I've bothered to reread is the sloppiness and shallowness of the worldbuilding. I think he did too much of the <em>wrong kind</em> of worldbuilding to lead to the sort of books I like - there's too much history and geography, and not enough character of any kind. So, for example, when we meet a secondary character, he ends up being a shallow collection of racial characteristics, because Eddings had a nice detailed list of what all the races were like - but no particular thought seems to have been given as to what individual <em>people</em> were like, outside of the main characters. And so we end up with a world that feels very shallow overall. And there are all sorts of minor bits of worldbuilding that end up getting retconned, because they were invented separately from the needs of the actual story.<br /><br />This is actually a book I would recommend to aspiring fantasists who are familiar with the Garion books, because I think it highlights many of the series's strengths and weaknesses. I don't necessarily think Eddings's advice should be followed without question, but that's true of all writing advice.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4918053445753890578">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_132865637">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132865637" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4466064-rob" class="left imgcol" title="Rob"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1405453454p2/4466064.jpg" alt="Rob" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/132865637?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 06, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4466064-rob" class="user" title="Rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4466064-rob?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer132865637">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11633608414067747936">I have been a fan of David Eddings ever since I read Pawn of Prophecy 20 years ago. I know that his books are derivative, repetitive, and obvious, but even with all this they are enjoyable and fun to read, rather easy and light.<br /><br />I have over the years added all the books from the Belgariad and Malloreon to my bookshelves at home. When I recently came across "The Rivan Codex" I wondered why I had never added this book, or even read it. I did recall seeing it in the book store when it was first publ</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11633608414067747936">I have been a fan of David Eddings ever since I read Pawn of Prophecy 20 years ago. I know that his books are derivative, repetitive, and obvious, but even with all this they are enjoyable and fun to read, rather easy and light.<br /><br />I have over the years added all the books from the Belgariad and Malloreon to my bookshelves at home. When I recently came across "The Rivan Codex" I wondered why I had never added this book, or even read it. I did recall seeing it in the book store when it was first published but could not recall why I ignored it.<br />After picking it up at the local library, (thankfully I did not spend any money on this tripe), and after reading through it I remember now why I avoided this book in the beginning. <br /><br />The book is based upon source material that was written when Eddings was developing the stories. Most of what is written here is not new and can be found in the Belgarath the Sorcerer and Polgara the Sorceress books. It is obvious that this material was written early and much of it not fully developed.<br /><br />Christoper Tolkien has published most if not all of the source material that his father wrote when developing his books. These are interesting and important to have because of Tolkien importance to this genre and literature in general. David Eddings even though his books are fun to read they are far from important. My thoughts are that this books release was unnecessary other then to drive revenue for the publisher</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11633608414067747936">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/7718219-chrys" class="user" title="'chrys">'chrys</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">"the collector/completionist"  </span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer276305588">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15885740840255498791">I both loved, and hated this book. <br /><br />I hated it because it wasn't actually a new 'story' and it wasn't really what the title suggested it would be to a fan of the two series. It wasn't bad though. It was interesting but it definitely was not a page turner. I read it slowly, over the course of several weeks where I typically devoured new Eddings novels in a single sitting. I reread the entire Belgariad and Malloreon while reading it and cross referenced between the novels and the 'text book' as I t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15885740840255498791">I both loved, and hated this book. <br /><br />I hated it because it wasn't actually a new 'story' and it wasn't really what the title suggested it would be to a fan of the two series. It wasn't bad though. It was interesting but it definitely was not a page turner. I read it slowly, over the course of several weeks where I typically devoured new Eddings novels in a single sitting. I reread the entire Belgariad and Malloreon while reading it and cross referenced between the novels and the 'text book' as I think of the Rivan Codex. <br /><br />I loved it because I found the world building intriguing. The autobiographical aspects pleased me because I'd always been a bit curious to know more about what made the author of some of my favorite books tick. There are parts that read like a text book and I'm not talking about the 'prologue' reprints. I'm just geeky enough that I -liked- those 'text book' moments. <br /><br />Definitely not for everyone. Don't read it first. Think of it as 'a guide to' and an autobiography lumped together. <br /><br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/9611342-jasmine-woods" class="left imgcol" title="Jasmine Woods"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1436561829p2/9611342.jpg" alt="Jasmine Woods" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/445064360?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9611342-jasmine-woods" class="user" title="Jasmine Woods">Jasmine Woods</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer445064360">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1555948756949386855">There are two reasons you'd think of read the Rivan Codex. The first is if you're a fan of the Belgariad (well, or the Malloreon, but they're much of a muchness) If this is the case you'll find plenty to love here. The rich detail Eddings put into creating how his world is admirable whilst the greatest enjoyment comes from seeing how his characters sprang up from his preliminary research. Despite this, even the most hard core fan might get bogged down somewhere between the Battle of Vo Mimbre an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1555948756949386855">There are two reasons you'd think of read the Rivan Codex. The first is if you're a fan of the Belgariad (well, or the Malloreon, but they're much of a muchness) If this is the case you'll find plenty to love here. The rich detail Eddings put into creating how his world is admirable whilst the greatest enjoyment comes from seeing how his characters sprang up from his preliminary research. Despite this, even the most hard core fan might get bogged down somewhere between the Battle of Vo Mimbre and the Book of Torak and do we really need to know how Tolnedran currency translates in Murgo when the information never even made it into the background of the series? Still, we have to applaud his lengthy efforts at attempting a realistic fantasy universe.<br /><br />The second reason you might pick this up is if you're an aspiring fantasy writer. If this is the case then Eddings has advice in spades. I didn't always agree with his methods, but for the most part his words are warm, witty and inspiring.<br /><br />An enjoyable read, but only the most dedicated need apply.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12602635699720670496">Maybe I wasnt a big enough fan of the Belgariad and Mallorean to get as much out of this as I could have, but this was only of middling enjoyability to read.<br /><br />It could be that almost everything in it, I had read before. Much of it repeatedly. It could be that the changing point of view or voice made much of it hard to swallow - for example - one ninute the voice of the book is telling us about creating the large sweeping back story, and the next minute the voice of the book is decrying the events in far off tales as unlikely to be true.<br />That is to say that the switching from macro universal voice to micro and back and forth repeatedly is at least a bit off putting.<br /><br />Still it isnt a total waste of time. If you liked reading the Belgariad and Mallorean, and wouldnt mind a taste, without re-reading the whole thing, and with some author insights thrown in for good measure, this might just be perfect for you.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3785889220560444538">If I was a truly cynical man I would be tempted to think that this is the literary equivalent of milking the cow to death. It removed any sense of the power of my imagination about the world inhabited by Belgarion; in fact the detail provided by the Eddings goes so far beyond what is required as to try and take control of my personal images.</span>

              <a href="/review/list/17852063-jamie-maltman?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer891963005">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13137465397544593297">I found this book on a cruise ship more than a decade after reading four series by Eddings. I found his process fascinating, and reading about it rekindled the world-building part of my mind, starting me on the path to finally publish my own fantasy books. <br /><br />So thank you late David Eddings for the enjoyment of your books as a teen, and thank you for the inspiration as an adult.<br /><br />Was the book that necessary for a fan of his world? More for the behind the scenes than for learning anything new.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/3494632-lori" class="user" title="Lori">Lori</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3494632-lori?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3494632-lori?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3494632-lori?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer116985931">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12179614344973209808">While openly written as a formulaic fantasy, the author(s) [David later credited his wife, Leigh, as being a co-writer for the series] still manage to make a compelling tale filled with vivacious characters who are interesting to follow wherever they will take you. This novel pulls together the Eddings' notes into a cohesive whole, showing where their famous series came from, both from the development of the different religions to the different races and areas.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_547474043">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547474043" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16066200-louis-carvalho" class="left imgcol" title="Louis Carvalho"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1357272281p2/16066200.jpg" alt="Louis Carvalho" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/547474043?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16066200-louis-carvalho" class="user" title="Louis Carvalho">Louis Carvalho</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer547474043">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9812048541248988843">This book gave a phenomenal look into the creative process behind the saga. Mr. Eddings goes into great detail on his world-building. Countries, rulers, caste systems, economics, clothing styles, imports and exports... You really see how he made the world of the Belgariad and the Mallorean come alive. It was easy because he gave life to the setting before he told a story within it. Brilliant and extremely useful for world-builders.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer136497513">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7485591318296805909">If you have read "The Belgarion" and "The Mallorean" series of fantasy books, you will enjoy this book. If not, don't bother. This is a collection of the background pieces that David Eddings wrote in preparation for writing his epic adventures. Very pleasant trip through the Holy Books of the gods, the Tolnedran histories and the Mallorean Gospels.</span>

          </span>

These men and women gifted with extraordinary mind powers are Chosen by, and bonded with, wondrous horse-like beings known as Companions. Brought by their Companions from the length and breadth of Valdemar to Haven, Valdemar\'s capital city, they are trained in a special school, the Collegium, and devote their lives to protecting king and kingdom. Mindspeakers, FarSeers, FarSpeakers, Firestarters, ForeSeers—their individual talents are as varied as their backgrounds. There are even those who can channel the magical nodes in the earth itself to use for their own purposes. Garbed in their uniforms of white leather, they patrol their territory, dispensing justice and keeping the peace. With the help and guidance of Mercedes Lackey, Helfers and Little have compiled a reader\'s guide to Mercedes Lackey\'s best-selling world of Valdemar.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings">About David Eddings</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/8732.David_Eddings"><img alt="8732" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1223870462p2/8732.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer2441634470500022224">David Eddings was an American author who has written several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, Leigh Eddings, is uncredited as co-author on many of his early books, but he has lately acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br /><br />David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2441634470500022224">David Eddings was an American author who has written several best-selling series of epic fantasy novels. David Eddings' wife, Leigh Eddings, is uncredited as co-author on many of his early books, but he has lately acknowledged that she contributed to them all.<br /><br />David Eddings' first books (which were general fiction) sold moderately well. He later switched to writing epic fantasy, a field in which he has achieved great success. In a recent interview with sffworld.com, he says: "I don't take orders from readers."<br /><br />On January 26, 2007 it was reported that Eddings accidentally burned about a quarter of his office, next door to his house, along with his Excalibur sports car, and the original manuscripts for most of his novels. He was flushing the fuel tank of the car with water when he lit a piece of paper and threw into the puddle to test if it was still flammable.<br /><br />On February 28, 2007, David Eddings' wife, Leigh Eddings (born Judith Leigh Schall), died following a series of strokes. She was 69.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2441634470500022224">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/938076-the-rivan-codex-ancient-texts-of-the-belgariad-and-the-malloreon">Trivia About The Rivan Codex: ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
				<p class="mediumText">No trivia or quizzes yet. <a href="/trivia/work/938076-the-rivan-codex-ancient-texts-of-the-belgariad-and-the-malloreon">Add some now »</a></p>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/938076-the-rivan-codex-ancient-texts-of-the-belgariad-and-the-malloreon">Quotes from The Rivan Codex: ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Operating by trial and error mostly, we've evolved a tacitly agreed upon list of the elements that make for a good fantasy. The first decision the aspiring fantasist must make is theological. King Arthur and Charlemagne were Christians. Siegfried and Sigurd the Volsung were pagans. My personal view is that pagans write better stories. When a writer is having fun, it shows, and pagans have more fun than Christians. Let's scrape Horace's Dulche et utile off the plate before we even start the banquet. We're writing for fun, not to provide moral instruction. I had much more fun with the Belgariad/Malloreon than you did, because I know where all the jokes are.<br /><br />All right, then, for item number one, I chose paganism. (Note that Papa Tolkien, a devout Anglo-Catholic, took the same route.)”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/421248-operating-by-trial-and-error-mostly-we-ve-evolved-a-tacitly" class="actionLinkLite">12 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Contemporary fantasists all bow politely to Lord Tennyson and Papa Tolkien, then step around them to go back to the original texts for inspiration--and there are a lot of those texts. We have King Arthur and his gang in English; we've got Siegfried and Brunhild in German; Charlemagne and Roland in French; El Cid in Spanish; Sigurd the Volsung in Icelandic; and assorted 'myghtiest Knights on lyfe' in a half-dozen other cultures. Without shame, we pillage medieval romance for all we're worth.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/421246-contemporary-fantasists-all-bow-politely-to-lord-tennyson-and-papa" class="actionLinkLite">9 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a href="/work/quotes/938076-the-rivan-codex-ancient-texts-of-the-belgariad-and-the-malloreon" style="float: right" class="actionLink">More quotes…</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
